## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and current population size. Classical population dynamics models express growth rates through density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms, ranging from simple exponential/logistic to more complex functional forms with Allee effects, harvesting, or time-dependent parameters.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (growth rate with logarithmic density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Cubic population model: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (strong Allee effect polynomial form)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance growth)
- Time-modulated exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting/immigration)
- Time-dependent logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (logistic with time-varying carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)
- Ricker-type rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (overcompensatory density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * P (rational density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality dP_dt ~ P → exponential (Malthusian) growth regime, density-independent
- Quadratic term P**2 in growth rate → density-dependent feedback (competition or cooperation among individuals)
- Product P*(K-P) structure → logistic-type carrying capacity with a stable equilibrium
- Negative cubic term -P**3 with positive P**2 → Allee effect with both lower and upper population thresholds
- Logarithmic dependence log(P) → Gompertz-type growth, slower deceleration near carrying capacity than logistic
- Exponential of P: exp(c*P) → Ricker-type overcompensation, sharper density regulation than polynomial
- Explicit time dependence in coefficients → non-autonomous system with changing environmental conditions
- Growth rate that changes sign at specific P values → equilibrium points (stable/unstable fixed points)
- Ratio P/(1+P) structure in growth → saturating per-capita resource acquisition (contest competition)
- Additive constant term independent of P → immigration, stocking, or constant harvesting pressure

$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the first part times P:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot [-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)]$$
$$= 0.1404 \cdot [-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(355.7)]$$

This gives us terms in P, P², P³, plus the $P/t^{4.532}$ term.

So GT = $a \cdot P^3 + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P + d \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$

where:
- $a = -0.1404/(4.532 \times 78.49) \approx -3.949 \times 10^{-4}$
- $b = 0.1404 \cdot (1/78.49 + 1/4.532) \approx 0.1404 \cdot 0.2334 \approx 0.03277$
- $c = -0.1404$
- $d = 0.1404$

The GT has the functional form: **$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P \cdot t^{-\kappa}$**

The key basis functions are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, and $P/t^{\kappa}$ (where $\kappa \approx 4.532$).

Now I need to check which candidates can match this. The critical term is $P/t^{4.532}$ — this is $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$, a power-law in $t$.

Let me check what functional forms the candidates use for the $t$-dependence:

Most candidates use $\exp(c \cdot t)$ for $t$-dependence, or polynomial terms like $t$, $t^2$. Some use $P^{c}$ which could give power-law behavior.

**Key observation:** $P/t^{4.532}$ is NOT equivalent to $P \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$ for any constant $c$. A power law in $t$ is fundamentally different from an exponential in $t$. Also, $P \cdot t$ (linear in $t$) cannot match $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$.

Let me look for candidates that have $P^{c_6}$ type terms (which could potentially be $P \cdot t^{-\kappa}$ if... no, that's power of P not t).

Wait - I need to look more carefully. None of the candidates seem to have $t^{c}$ as a basis function. Let me re-examine.

Looking at candidates with $P^{c_6}$ terms: these are power-law in P, not in t.

The GT requires $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$. No candidate has a $t^{c}$ term. The candidates use:
- $\exp(c \cdot t)$: exponential in t
- $c \cdot t$: linear in t  
- $t^2$: quadratic in t
- $t \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$

None of these can produce $t^{-4.532}$. An exponential cannot equal a power law for all $t$. Linear/polynomial $t$ cannot equal $t^{-4.532}$.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because none contain the basis function $t^{-\kappa}$ (power-law in $t$).

Let me verify this conclusion by checking every candidate... All 50 candidates use combinations of $\exp(c \cdot t)$, $t$, $t^2$, $t \cdot \exp(c \cdot t)$ for $t$-dependence, or $\log(\cdot)$ terms. None have $t^{c}$ or $1/t^{c}$ as a standalone basis function. The $P^{c_6}$ terms are powers of $P$, not $t$.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
